< Text>
The Juice It Up in the food court closed down not too long ago, so in my search for an afternoon smoothie, I stumbled upon this little restaurant. The smoothies themselves seem to be sold in one size- more than enough to oversupply one with sugar for a day. But every sip was very tasty, and the staff were very quick to prepare it. The sandwiches here were great as well, but a little bit on the pricey side. The seating arrangement was rather comfortable, with a sort of bar along the counter as well as chairs dotted along the edges of the floor.<//Text>

<text>***UPDATE***
While I was forced to involve a regulatory agency to resolve this matter, I was finally reimbursed for the damages. It's not the damaged piece that's disappointing, it's the fact they denied the damage - when they were clearly at fault.

Original review:
TL;DR: If your vehicle is damaged by Tigris Auto Glass in any way you will be made a mockery of and the owner will not acknowledge responsibility. If you look through other customer feedback regarding Tigris, it mirrors my experience. Some speak to various levels of damage done while in their care. Most, if not all of these examples were left unresolved. I STRONGLY recommend you avoid doing business with Tigris under any circumstances. There are plenty of other auto glass options in the greater Sacramento area. I would venture to say most, if not all, will treat you better, should the unthinkable happen.

On 6/6/20, 9:00 AM, I arrived at Tigris for a windshield replacement. I chose this location based on public feedback, (4.5 stars on Yelp, 4.4 on Google reviews). The vehicle was immediately taken to the shop in the back of the building. There was no vehicle check-in, vehicle condition report, or authorization of work to be performed prior to the installation. The vehicle was completed in approx 60-75 minutes. Without any presentation of work performed, I was given the keys to the car in the office/lobby, without being offered the option to review their work. Only after paying for the work, were the keys relinquished. When I walked outside to perform an initial walkaround of the vehicle, no significant damage was noted. No curbed wheels, no dented doors. It was only when I stopped at the gas station (at 10:28 AM), did I notice the plastic piece surrounding the A¬≠-pillar on the driver-side of the vehicle was cracked. I know this was not present prior to the installation of the glass because I had performed a thorough automotive detail on the vehicle myself. The passenger side panel was also loose and not fully seated. I immediately returned to the place of business (11:01 AM) and presented my concern to the assistant, Monica in the office. She immediately notified the business owner, who followed me, outside to-discuss. He was immediately defensive and argumentative, stating this was already cracked, and that by lifting this panel from the bottom, this could not have happened in their care. The technician responsible for the installation soon appeared and too argued that he was not responsible for the damage. The carpet on the driver's side of the vehicle had a substantial amount of water. This is a key piece of evidence because while they were washing the windshield area, they contaminated the crack in question. Whether intentional or not, this gave the fresh cracks an "aged" look. They presented this "old crack, it's dirty" as an argument for their defense. After a 15 minute discussion in the parking lot, the owner initially agreed to remedy the situation by obtaining a replacement piece from Ford. I was later contacted on 6/9 by Monica of Tigris and they confirmed this item is unavailable and asked that I obtain a quote at a body shop to have it repaired. I obtained and provided Tigris a quote in the amount of $249 from AutoBody Expressions, in Elk Grove. After review, the owner refused to pay the $249 and asked that I surrender my car to his "friend's body shop", and he would cover the repair. Otherwise, he would only pay half of Autobody Expressions' estimate. I will not trust my mint condition Mustang to a business I, myself, do not have a personal relationship with. When I was given this information, I countered with providing 2 more (for a total of 3) estimates. Those have come in at $431, from Caliber Collision, and finally a third in the amount of $328, from Bertolluci's, in Sacramento. The third quote was provided to the business owner on 6/16/20. I have also filed a complaint with the Better Business Bureau, which is still under investigation. As of 6/26, I have not received any contact from Tigris resolving this outstanding issue.</text>< Rate>
